  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_903c33e3-8338-44dd-8e19-24540f1b85cd'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

Dom</span>
  <span id="freeText14533317041426997435" style="display:none">After a car accident killed her parents when she was a child, Bronagh Murphy chose to box herself off from people in an effort to keep herself from future hurt. If she doesn't befriend people, talk to them or acknowledge them in any way they leave her alone just like she wants. <br /><br />When Dominic Slater enters her life, ignoring him is all she has to do to get his attention. Dominic is used to attention, and when he and his brothers move to Dublin, Ireland for family business, he gets nothing but attention. Attention from everyone except the beautiful brunette with a sharp tongue. <br /><br />Dominic wants Bronagh and the only way he can get to her, is by dragging her from the boxed off corner she has herself trapped in the only way he knows how... by force. <br /><br />Dominic wants her, and what Dominic wants, Dominic gets.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/884334445?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer884334445" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18419174550584187332">QUOTES ARE FROM THE "READER'S NOTE" AT THE START OF THE BOOK<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"Dominic is set in Ireland; most of the characters are Irish, and the Irish have a dialect that is completely different from any other dialect in the world. We tend to break words down when speaking and jumble them….."</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395253669i/8972538._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395253669i/8972539.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"I want to make it clear that when you see an Irish character in Dominic say the word “me” where “my” should be, that is supposed to be written that way. Everything is “me” here in Ireland and rarely “my”… "</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395253669i/8972538._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"…we</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText18419174550584187332" style="display:none">QUOTES ARE FROM THE "READER'S NOTE" AT THE START OF THE BOOK<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Dominic is set in Ireland; most of the characters are Irish, and the Irish have a dialect that is completely different from any other dialect in the world. We tend to break words down when speaking and jumble them….."</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395253669i/8972538._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395253669i/8972539.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I want to make it clear that when you see an Irish character in Dominic say the word “me” where “my” should be, that is supposed to be written that way. Everything is “me” here in Ireland and rarely “my”… "</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395253669i/8972538._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"…we also leave out the letter G on most words when we speak, again, this is just another part of our dialect.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395253669i/8972538._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I just wanted to put this note in for readers who aren’t familiar with Irish dialect, so you don’t read a sentence and think “WTF?”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>How about putting a note for those of us who ARE Irish and are familiar with Irish dialect and think WTF?<br><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395254104i/8972562._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I only read the sample and that was enough for me. Seriously, as an Irish person I was disturbed by the way we were portrayed. Even the fucking teacher in the school couldn’t pronounce the words. The author is from Dublin. I am not, but I do know Dublin people and I know they also would be horrified to be portrayed like that.<br><br>So any of my friends who read this book, please, please be under no illusions that we are ALL like that from Ireland.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>That’s ME desk<br>… drive ME crazy …<br>… that’s ME name.<br>… can I listen to ME Itouch?<br>He’s in ME seat.<br>… share ME worktop.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>… and that was only in the sample.<br><br>OK, I might be a bit notorious on here for flying the flag for Ireland and have given harsh reviews to non-Irish authors for not doing it right. But when it is one of your own that cannot get it right, that is a NO GO area for me. <br><br>I wish the author well. It is a debut novel but doubt you will have many Irish fans!! Then again I could be completely wrong. Its been 25 years since I lived in the country...</span>
  <a data-text-id="18419174550584187332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

So for sake of my sanity and my beloved ereader, I’m singing off this shit.   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/871120033?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❥ KAT ❥ Kitty Kats Crazy About Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❥ KAT ❥ Kitty Kats Crazy About Books" href="/user/show/6245313-kat-kitty-kats-crazy-about-books">❥ KAT ❥ Kitty Kats Crazy About Books</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer871120033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15662491460156869371"><b>5 Shockingly Good Fuck-Face and Fat-Arse Stars</b><br/><br/><a href='http://tinypic.com?ref=1zd97qv' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394240198i/8827060._SX540_.jpg' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>ARC Provided by the author, "L.A.Casey" in exchange for an honest review</b><br/><br/><b>"RAMPAGE"</b><br/><br/><a href='http://tinypic.com?ref=2nknwj6' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394240198ra/8827061.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>

<span id="freeTextContainer15971154146532608036"><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <a href='http://www.amazon.com/dp/B00J1SP9FI' rel='nofollow noopener'>AMAZON US</a>

  <a href='http://www.scribd.com/book/230834754' rel='nofollow noopener'>SCRIBD</a>
  <br/>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/><b>READERS NOTE</b><br/><i>DOMINIC</i> is set in Ireland; most of the characters are Irish, and the Irish have a dialect that is completely different from any other dialect in the world. We tend to break words down when speaking and jumble them up; we're weird like that.<br/><br/>I want to make it clear that when you see an Irish (Dublin) character in <i>DOMINIC</i> and the rest of the <i>Slater Brothers</i> series know that they are based on my accent and how I speak, when</span>
  <span id="freeText15971154146532608036" style="display:none"><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <a href="http://www.amazon.com/dp/B00J1SP9FI" rel="nofollow noopener">AMAZON US</a>
  <br />
  <a href="http://www.amazon.co.uk/dp/B00J1SP9FI" rel="nofollow noopener">AMAZON UK</a>
  <br />
  <a href="http://tinyurl.com/khvhnn7" rel="nofollow noopener">KOBO</a>
  <br />
  <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/us/book/id892223155" rel="nofollow noopener">ITUNES</a>
  <br />
  <a href="http://www.scribd.com/book/230834754" rel="nofollow noopener">SCRIBD</a>
  <br />
</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><b>READERS NOTE</b><br /><i>DOMINIC</i> is set in Ireland; most of the characters are Irish, and the Irish have a dialect that is completely different from any other dialect in the world. We tend to break words down when speaking and jumble them up; we're weird like that.<br /><br />I want to make it clear that when you see an Irish (Dublin) character in <i>DOMINIC</i> and the rest of the <i>Slater Brothers</i> series know that they are based on my accent and how I speak, when they say the word 'me' where 'my' should be, it is <b>supposed</b> to be written that way. Of course, not <i>everyone</i> in Ireland says 'me' in replacement of 'my', this is again just based on my own accent and how I speak. I replace 'my' with 'me' nearly 100% of the time.<br /> <br />Here in South Dublin, where the book is set, it is also more common for <i>most</i> people (<b>not everyone!</b>) to leave out the letter G on <i>most</i> words when they speak, again, this is just another part of our dialect.<br /><br />I just wanted to put this note in for readers who aren't familiar with Irish dialect, so you don't read a sentence and think, "What the fuck?"<br /><br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/885416504?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tori" href="/user/show/3094317-tori">Tori</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094317-tori?shelf=violence">violence</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094317-tori?shelf=bad-boy-bad-boy-what-ya-gonna-do">bad-boy-bad-boy-what-ya-gonna-do</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094317-tori?shelf=i-can-t-stop-reading-this-crap">i-can-t-stop-reading-this-crap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094317-tori?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094317-tori?shelf=dealing-with-grief">dealing-with-grief</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer885416504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2137631074689264862">Oy.<br/><br/>I'm not really even sure where to start with this book. I read the warning attached to the book claiming there is abundance of cursing, alpha behavior, and OTT drama. However, Ms. Casey fails to inform the reader there is bullying, slut shaming, gratuitous violence, and an emotionally abusive relationship. Oh yes, no matter how many times you giggle during this book, the relationship between the MCs is abusive. <br/><br/>Similar to Beautiful Disaster in the set up-bad boy who illegally fights and is us</span>
  <span id="freeText2137631074689264862" style="display:none">Oy.<br /><br />I'm not really even sure where to start with this book. I read the warning attached to the book claiming there is abundance of cursing, alpha behavior, and OTT drama. However, Ms. Casey fails to inform the reader there is bullying, slut shaming, gratuitous violence, and an emotionally abusive relationship. Oh yes, no matter how many times you giggle during this book, the relationship between the MCs is abusive. <br /><br />Similar to Beautiful Disaster in the set up-bad boy who illegally fights and is used to getting what he wants meets a good girl who is emotionally cut off from the world and rejects him and his love. <br /><br />Sadly, it's all down hill from there. We watch as the hero bullies, insults, and sexually assaults the heroine to show her he likes her. Wait, it gets better. His gives voice to his attraction by calling her a phat arse (that's suppose to be a complement), slut, crazy bitch, and my personal fav...c*nt.<br /> <br />Be still my heart. <br /><br />The heroine is no better. She's belligerent, verbally and physically abusive to him in return. She makes her feelings known repeatedly that she wants nothing to do with him yet after he beats up a boy who she's friends with for the 3rd time she decides to try being his girlfriend because why fight fate. *head desk* . I think what cheesed me off more then anything is his and her family saw nothing wrong with the way they acted. They just poo pooed and brushed it off because that was just the way this couple is, ya know? No, I don't know. I don't want to know.<br /><br />I know this review sounds frivolous but it's really not. This book is so anti romance it isn't even funny. If you looking for a how to manual on abusive YA relationships then here you go. If your looking for a YA romance that celebrates young love and healthy relationships then I suggest you skip this one. <br /><br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="2137631074689264862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_821227340" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer821227340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8918189338544549821">*******************************************************<br/><br/>If you're a prude, <b>DO NOT READ THIS BOOK.</b><br/>If you can't handle a hero and heroine who are batshit crazy, <b>DO NOT READ THIS BOOK.</b><br/>If you can't handle swearing, violence and a bunch of random stuff been thrown at the hero's head, <b>SERIOUSLY, DO NOT READ THIS BOOK.</b><br/>If you <b>DON'T</b> heed the author's warning and go ahead and read the book <b>KNOWING</b> you will hate what is in the warnings then you my friend, are a special kind of stupid.<br/><br/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>BASED ON <i>MOST</i> OF 1 S</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8918189338544549821" style="display:none">*******************************************************<br><br>If you're a prude, <b>DO NOT READ THIS BOOK.</b><br>If you can't handle a hero and heroine who are batshit crazy, <b>DO NOT READ THIS BOOK.</b><br>If you can't handle swearing, violence and a bunch of random stuff been thrown at the hero's head, <b>SERIOUSLY, DO NOT READ THIS BOOK.</b><br>If you <b>DON'T</b> heed the author's warning and go ahead and read the book <b>KNOWING</b> you will hate what is in the warnings then you my friend, are a special kind of stupid.<br><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>BASED ON <i>MOST</i> OF 1 STAR REVIEWS, TOO MANY PEOPLE ARE IGNORING THE AUTHOR'S WARNINGS ABOUT THE VIOLENCE, LANGUAGE AND DRAMA WITHIN THE BOOK AND ARE <i>STILL</i> GOING AHEAD AND READING IT ANYWAY THEN GIVING A SHITTY REVIEW FOR THINGS THAT THE AUTHOR WARNED THEM WOULD BE IN THE BOOK. WHY READ SOMETHING YOU KNOW CONTAINS THINGS YOU HATE?</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>I will <b>NEVER</b> base a book off reviews <b>EVER AGAIN</b>. Some of the reviews for Dominic on this page are fucking <b>APPALLING</b>. I was ticked off after reading many of them because I bought the book and was bummed it would be a bad read because that is was all the negative reviews promise. <br><br><b>HOW ABOUT LETTING PEOPLE DECIDE FOR THEMSELVES WHAT THEY LIKE!</b> <br><br>It seems I was the minority that actually read the author's warning and readers note in her review, it wasn't hard to miss, it's on top of the fucking page <b>AND</b> on the description of the book on Amazon. I honestly do <b>NOT</b> understand why everyone is bitching about the drama, violence and constant swearing when they were fucking <b>TOLD</b> it would be in the book. I don't get it at all. Either they managed to miss the warnings that were in the description or they are plain fucking stupid! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395326818i/8979934.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br>********************************************************<br><br><b>UPDATE:</b> This <i>DEBUT</i> book was released on March 17th, 2014 and today March 20th, 2014, three days after its release, it is an Amazon Bestseller!! The author is only 22 years old, still a kid, with her whole life and career ahead of her, congratulations to you L.A. Casey, I wish you nothing but success!<br><br>********************************************************<br><br><br>I <b>LOVED</b> the book, the warnings actually appealed to me which is why I bought the book. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395326681i/8979920.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I thought it started off very YA but that went straight out the window and after a few chapters it was easy to see why it is New Adult and not straight up Young Adult. The characters are 18 and deal with a lot of shit.<br><br>I came across this little gem on the movers and shakers list on Amazon and I am really happy I took a chance on it because <b>HELLO SLATER BROTHERS!!! </b><br><br>The best way for me to start this review is to declare my love for Dominic, Nico, Fuckface, Rampage or whatever the fuck you want to call him and claim him as <b>mine!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380426311ra/851724.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> I love <i>everything</i> about this character, I surprisingly even love the fact that he is a <i>huge</i> asshole who says the word 'fuck' more times than a nun says prayers. Usually that would get on my nerves but the fact that Dominic's character was not only possessive and dominant, but was also funny, sarcastic and a sweetheart really did it for me and helped balance out a lot of the shit he did. Don't get me wrong, I wanted to slap him silly at times when he treated Bronagh badly but I couldn't help but love him because he made up for all the bad things he did. He is my new number one book boyfriend friend, Ms Casey knocked it out the park with this character. <br><br><i>Dominic</i> is L.A. Casey's <b>DEBUT NOVEL</b> and she completely killed it, I'm so excited for the rest of the series! Bring on the rest of the Slater brothers, mama is ready for you! <br><br><i>Dominic</i> isn't about just a book about meaningless fighting, sex and teenage/adult drama. While it does have a lot of those things, being <b>meaningful</b> of course, the main aspects of the story are loyalty and letting go. Loyalty is mainly between the Slater brothers in this story. Ryder, Kane, Alec, Dominic and Damien make up this sexy as sin family. I won't give away any spoilers but when you find out the things they go through you will understand why they are so loyal and would do anything for one another. I <b>LOVED</b> that, I loved how close the brothers are and the fact that would literally die for each other without a seconds hesitation is just... ugh!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386938042ra/7486772.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The letting go aspect of the book is for our leading lady, Bronagh Murphy, and for one of the Slater brothers but you will have to read to find out who ;)<br><br>Bronagh (Pronounced Bro-nah) is in a bubbled world, a world she created herself by never letting anyone inside. She fears rejection and loss, the death of her parents when she was young enabled these feelings inside her and moulded her into the iron hearted person she is. She is an angry person, and even though she snapped at Dominic for things that most people would let slide, she has every right to be, she lost her parents when she was a child, that would mess anyone's head up. The only person she keeps close to her is her older sister/guardian, Branna. <br><br>Bronagh is the definition of a loner, but certainly not a push over. I <b>LOVED</b> that about her, I honestly thought she would be a bullied girl and that Dominic would stand up for her, thus entering her life but that is <b>SO</b> not what happens. Bronagh may be a loner and an all round quiet person in general but if you step to her, you best believe she will come out swinging... literally. She doesn't like talking to people or dealing with people in anyway and when she has to, depending on the situation, she will be nice and polite or downright feisty and rude.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391635939ra/8423522.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Dominic and his brothers come to her hometown in Dublin, Ireland, it kicks off the roller coaster of a ride that is their relationship. From that point on we're apart of a love/hate relationship between two characters who lust after one another like crazy but at times (most of the time) can't stand each other. Dominic is not your typical hard headed 18 year old, he is determined person with very grown up job. A <b>secret</b> job and is right up my fucking street. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395346414ra/8983053.gif" width="380" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Will Bronagh succeed at pushing Dominic away or will this arrogant stud find a way to teach her what it is really like to live and open your heart to the possibilities of love? Read to find out! <br><br>I was constantly surprised while reading Dominic, I <b>loved</b> that the plot line wasn't predictable. It was such a refreshing read after reading so many heartbreaking books over the last few weeks. Seriously, I laughed so hard during some scenes while reading that I got cramps!!. The reason why the brothers were in Ireland excited me so much more because I wasn't expecting it, I mean, I had an slight idea from Bronagh's suspicions but nothing like what was actually happening. That alone has me so excited for the rest of the books in the series because I have <i>no</i> idea what direction the author will take the other brothers books it but I am so ready to dive head first into them and find out!<br><br><b>I'M SO EXCITED!!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380429718ra/860998.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><br><br><b>P.S. To the people who one starred the book when they sampled it or marked as DNF.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397679698ra/9310733.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <a href="http://www.amazon.com/dp/B00J1SP9FI" rel="nofollow noopener">Dominic on Amazon</a>
  <br>
  <a href="https://www.amazon.co.uk/dp/B00J1SP9FI" rel="nofollow noopener">Dominic on Amazon UK</a>
</blockquote></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16773103595664309584">So I'll admit that this started off a little rough! <br/><br/>If you're not a fan of assholes with no limits to what they can and can't do, can and can't say then don't read this. You'll cringe. But I'm the kind of girl that really loves an <b>ASSHOLE ALPHA</b> and I freaking loveeeedddd this. There was just so much juiciness. Yes, they're a little immature but they're in high school!!! There's a lot of dirty language but again it didn't bother me in the slightest. I got more annoyed at the slap happiness at one</span>
  <span id="freeText16773103595664309584" style="display:none">So I'll admit that this started off a little rough! <br /><br />If you're not a fan of assholes with no limits to what they can and can't do, can and can't say then don't read this. You'll cringe. But I'm the kind of girl that really loves an <b>ASSHOLE ALPHA</b> and I freaking loveeeedddd this. There was just so much juiciness. Yes, they're a little immature but they're in high school!!! There's a lot of dirty language but again it didn't bother me in the slightest. I got more annoyed at the slap happiness at one point but then it died down. By the time I got to the end I was in <b>LOVVVVVVVE</b> with <b>EVERY CHARACTER!</b> <br /><br />I can't wait for the next one! <br /><br />I especially <b>LOVVVVVED</b> the Irish lingo! Gah! I just felt like I was in Ireland! Lovedddd it. <br /><br />Oh and the sex....<b>HOTTTTTTTT!</b> I mean he's 18 and Holy Moses! I can just imagine what a monster he'll be at thirty lol! <br /><br />Also, I found this to be such a <b>GOOD</b> story plot wise. <b>LOTS</b> of action, funny at times, nutty at times, sexy at times. It was just an <b>ALL</b> out <b>GREAT</b> time. <br /><br /><b>BUT REALLY BEWARE THESE CHARACTERS ARE FUCKING NUTS.</b> Hahahahaha! But I <b>LOVED</b> living in there <b>NUTTY</b> world. Oh and if you don't like the girl being called, bitch or slut, then think on this. I mean, sometimes it's said mean but other times it's funny and jokish. <b>AGAIN</b>, I am <b>NOT</b> offended by things like that as long as the tone is not condescending and belittling. It's just all a matter of taste (IMO)!!! :) </span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer873271648" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18346076132739094576"><b>

  <i>Dominc</i>

  <i>Dominic</i>
</b> tells the story of two individuals at a crossroads with life.<br/><br/>Set in the lavish suburbs of Irel</span>
  <span id="freeText18346076132739094576" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>UPDATE:</u>
</b> It's LIVE on <a href="http://www.amazon.co.uk/Dominic-Slater-Brothers-L-A-Casey-ebook/dp/B00J1SP9FI/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1395019010&amp;sr=8-1&amp;keywords=dominic+l.a.+casey" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon UK</a>, <a href="http://www.amazon.com/dp/B00J1SP9FI" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon US</a>, and <a href="https://www.amazon.com.au/dp/B00J1SP9FI" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon AU</a> friends!! Pick up your copy NOW!!<br><br><b>Holy fuc#%in sh*t this book was not what I had expected!</b><br><br>~And why yes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/871120033?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Kat,</a> “Blonde Twin is Amazing!” F*#k, I LOVED Damien!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394750356i/8900785._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>Dominc</i>
</b> was a nice interlude to kick off the stories of the Slater brothers, all FIVE of them, and their relationships with their women and trying to take hold of their pasts. <br><br><b>
  <i>Dominic</i>
</b> tells the story of two individuals at a crossroads with life.<br><br>Set in the lavish suburbs of Ireland, we meet one feisty Irish gal and one American underground fighter looking to have a fresh start.<br><br>Bronagh (pronounced “Bro-nah” my fellow non-Irish friends) Murphy, lost her parents at a very young age which left big sister Branna as her guardian and rock for all extents and purposes. Due to this loss, Bronagh closes herself off and won’t let anyone get close to her with the exception of big sis.<br><br>She meets American transfer students (yes, they are still in high school!) Dominic “Nico” Slater and his twin Damien, and her world is forever shifted upside down. And no, there is no love triangle between her and the two bro’s. There’s other suitor’s vying for the attentions of Bronagh and Nico but no love triangles! Thank god!<br><br>Now faced with the only person who can bring her outside of her shell will she succumb to Dominic’s iron will and give him and life a chance? And will Dominic ever win over the girl that is so different from the others and challenges him at every turn? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394750657i/8900864.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But with a secret dwindling down that threatens to tear apart everything and could mean deadly consequences, how will everything turn out?<br><br><b>
  <u>My verdict:</u>
</b> <b>An awesome beginning of what’s to come!</b><br> <br><b>
  <i>Dominic,</i>
</b> is filled with everything from: love, renewal, anguish, deceit, letting go and giving into second chances!<br><br>I wished that book two would have been on Damien, the “nice” twin that Brongah always refers to but sadly his story won’t be till last! How did I know?! Always save the most anticipated stories to the end!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394751119ra/8900904.gif" width="400" height="226" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Instead, book two will focus on Alec, one of Dominic and Damien’s older brothers and it looks to be an interesting one!! Especially because Alec is a ******(no spoiler!)! <br><br>Then after we have Kane, Ryder, and lastly Damien.<br><br>I really hope that for Ryder’s story that there isn’t additional drama to his and (*I’m not spoiling)’s story! I thought they were awesome together in <b>
  <i>Dominic</i>
</b> and so if there’s any unnecessary developments that lead to a break up, cheating, or moving on to others I will throw a serious tantrum and turn into a Bronagh and whack some people in the head!<br><br>And that brings me to another thing! Do all Irish have tempers?! Bronagh and her sister were such a riot and were always quick to flare up and mob someone! Woah. But in another sense, I have to admit that it was kind of funny and entertaining. <br><br>As for Dominic, he too had a temper but nothing like Bronagh. His overprotective and possessive as well as alpha male tendencies were tremendous factors as to his character and his love/hate relationship with Bronagh. I swear, they were 99% of the book bickering and Bronagh was always delivering some kind of physical blow to his body.<br><br>And let’s not forget their nicknames for each other: Bronagh=”Pretty girl” or “Fat-Arse” and Dominic is “F*#k Face”. Such lovely endearments! Lol<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394751119i/8900905._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>In conclusion:</u>
</b> I DEFINITELY recommend this to you girls who dig dominant strong men! I will caution that like I was warned by the author, the main girl is quite the b*tch and the main guy is a prick.<br><br>HOWEVER, it still didn’t defer me from loving it all the way and reading this book straight in two sessions! I was that addicted! L.A. Casey sure writes quite an explosive beginning to the start of something great!<br><br><b>Gosh, I want book two already!!</b><br><br><i>*An ARC was provided to me via the author for an honest review. Thank you!*</i></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_882136043" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/882136043" />
    <a title="~ Becs ~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2626261-becs"><img alt="~ Becs ~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388693144p2/2626261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/882136043?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~ Becs ~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~ Becs ~" href="/user/show/2626261-becs">~ Becs ~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=sports-star-hero">sports-star-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=cover-lust-i-has-it">cover-lust-i-has-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=shy-heroine">shy-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=small-town-romance">small-town-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer882136043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17729589017868354034"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395083013i/8944126._SX540_.jpg' alt=' photo dominiccasting_zps9c055d68.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Well, it’s safe to say that this book is a complete RIOT! It’s totally not what I was expecting. When I first saw that cover and read the blurb, I was expecting a romance in a similar style to Katy Evans’ Real but this is very different from that. In fact, when I first realised that the two main protagonists are actually in High School, I was initially a little put off, but there’s something about this book that really kind of captivated me and I was pretty much sucked in.<br/><br/>Let me start off by say</span>
  <span id="freeText17729589017868354034" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395083013i/8944126._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo dominiccasting_zps9c055d68.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, it’s safe to say that this book is a complete RIOT! It’s totally not what I was expecting. When I first saw that cover and read the blurb, I was expecting a romance in a similar style to Katy Evans’ Real but this is very different from that. In fact, when I first realised that the two main protagonists are actually in High School, I was initially a little put off, but there’s something about this book that really kind of captivated me and I was pretty much sucked in.<br><br>Let me start off by saying that this book is VERY Irish - you can hear that Irish Brogue coming through loud and clear with the attitude, the slang and the swearing. No one can swear quite like the Irish – I feckin’ love it! I think it’s incredibly fitting that the book releases on Paddy’s Day – perfect timing.<br><br>Bronagh is our heroine, who has been raised for nine years by her elder sister due the tragic loss of her parents. This has hit Bronagh hard and she’s vowed never to allow anyone close enough to her for her to ever feel that pain of loss ever again. She’s closed off from everyone apart from Bronagh and hides from reality behind a pair of ear buds staying in her own little world. She’s incredibly spiky and practically snarls at anyone who gets close – she’s funny but she’s also very sharp with a dry,acerbic wit. Most of all, Bronagh is fierce, scarily so – she has a short fuse and is never shy of standing up for herself and what she thinks is right.<br><br>The American Slater Brothers storm into town like a tornado and Dominic and Damien, totally gorgeous twins, are placed in Bronagh’s class and Dominic knows straight away that he wants her but she’s gong to make it as difficult for him as she possibly can, fighting off his charms while other girls are literally falling at his feet but he is determined to pursue her.<br><br>Dominic is cocky, arrogant, possessive, protective, rude, quick to anger but he’s also incredibly charming and lovable, as are all the Slater boys and, despite some of his absolute stupidity in this book, he’s hard not to like. He torments Bronagh at school for ignoring his advances and makes her life hell. I had to laugh when he admired her ‘phat ass’ and she thought he had said ‘fat arse’ and named him Fuckface – they really did become Fatarse and Fuckface in my head after that one and I found myself grinning like a goof at some of their antics and arguments.<br><br>This is all kinds of crazy as the story thunders along at a furious pace with everyone constantly falling out, snarling and hissing at one another like feral cats and constantly falling into physical fights. I think I lost count of the amount of times poor old Dominic got clocked around the head. Luckily, the guy has a hard head as he’s an underground fighter going by the names of Nico or Rampage, something that Bronagh really doesn’t like.<br><br>Of course, there’s a reason why the Slater Brothers have come to Ireland and this will come roaring back to put them all in danger and the last part of the novel is a crazy rush of drama and action and it really does move us well beyond the High School style romance and into something significantly more adult. <br><br>I have to say Bronagh’s High School experience is pretty brutal. She gets beaten up several times and is always finding herself embroiled in fights and Dominic is no better – both of them, and several others, spend most of this novel wandering around with cuts and bruises.<br><br>Deep at the heart of the novel, despite the batshit crazy pace, is a story of deep and abiding loyalty between family and friends and very much a strong theme of love – brotherly, sisterly, romantic and very sexual love. It’s thoroughly enjoyable and charming with some really great character development. It’s so sweet to see Bronagh’s spiky resolve slowly being taken down by Dominic and her frozen heart slowly melting for him. I adored the way that he loved her and cherished her, despite their screaming arguments and I couldn’t help but find myself rooting for them.<br><br><blockquote>"I'm yours?" I mumbled, still in awe that this beautiful person wanted me when he could have any girl he wanted.<br><br>Dominic smiled at me and kissed the tip of my nose then winked as he said, "You've always been mine, pretty girl. You just didn't know it."</blockquote><br><br>This book is just all kinds of crazy but, strangely, it works – OK, it’s a debut and it’s a little rough around the edges with a few typos but it’s very original and it is absolutely hilarious and I really did enjoy it and I’ll definitely be continuing with the series. Can’t wait for some more Slater Boys action with Alec, the manwhore, up next. I’m dying for Damien’s story which I think will be the most emotional but it appears the author is saving the best till last.<br><br>4 totally mad stars<br><br><p><a href="http://sinfullysexybooks.blogspot.co.uk/2014/03/dominic-by-la-casey-release-day-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Read this review at Sinfully Sexy</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/sinfullysexybookreviews" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow us on Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/SinfullySexyB" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow us on Twitter</a></p></span>
  <a data-text-id="17729589017868354034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10014119678115203711"><strong>Fighting, bickering, jealousy, love-hate, funny goodness!</strong><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1583330194i/29055593._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book was quite a ride from beginning to end. Bronagh is an Irish girl who lost her parents at a young age and lives with her older sister. She decided when she lost her parents that she wouldn’t form any other relationships because it hurt too much to lose them. So she keeps completely to herself in school and in her life aside from her sister.<br/><br/>When Americans Dominic and Damien start at her school, Dominic is immediately intrigued by t</span>
  <span id="freeText10014119678115203711" style="display:none"><strong>Fighting, bickering, jealousy, love-hate, funny goodness!</strong><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1583330194i/29055593._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was quite a ride from beginning to end. Bronagh is an Irish girl who lost her parents at a young age and lives with her older sister. She decided when she lost her parents that she wouldn’t form any other relationships because it hurt too much to lose them. So she keeps completely to herself in school and in her life aside from her sister.<br><br>When Americans Dominic and Damien start at her school, Dominic is immediately intrigued by the girl who wants nothing to do with him. He won’t leave her alone and though she likes to keep to herself, when she is antagonized, she gives as good as she gets.<br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“IthinkIbrokeyourXboxbutIdidn’tmeantoIswear,” I blurted out in one breath. <br>Dominic just stared at me for a moment, and then slowly set me down onto my feet. “Move so I can check on her,” he growled. <br>I widened my eyes for two reasons. Firstly, he actually understood my rapid-fire admission, and secondly he called his Xbox her.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br>What starts out as a hate-hate relationship between Bronagh and Dominic changes a bit when one of the other boys starts pushing her around and Dominic stands up for her and fights him saying that the guy touched what was his. From there it turns into a love-hate relationship between the two main characters.<br><br>They go back and forth trying to figure out their feelings, while she is still dealing with her issues. It is a definite roller coaster ride but I loved it. Dominic had feelings for her from the start and he gets possessive and jealous and keeps messing things up, but he has a good heart. I plan to read the whole series.<br><br><a href="https://www.ilikebooksbest.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a>|<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/wennel" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a>|<a href="https://www.facebook.com/ilikebooksbest" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>|<a href="https://www.instagram.com/ilikebooksbest" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a>|<a href="https://www.twitter.com/wendysu020202" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>|<a href="https://www.bookbub.com/profile/1895823057" rel="nofollow noopener">BookBub</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15826381475930704015">2.5 stars<br/><br/><b>BLURB:</b> Orphaned at a young age, eighteen year old Bronagh is used to keeping people at a distance, afraid to let anyone in and eventually get hurt. That all changes the day the hot American Dominic walks into her school and is constantly in her face. Everywhere she turns, he's there, annoying the fuck out of her. Of course, that can only mean one thing...<br/><br/>- - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - -<br/><br/>I had a ton of issues with this book. It really was <b>not for me.</b> Mostly th</span>
  <span id="freeText15826381475930704015" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br /><b>BLURB:</b> Orphaned at a young age, eighteen year old Bronagh is used to keeping people at a distance, afraid to let anyone in and eventually get hurt. That all changes the day the hot American Dominic walks into her school and is constantly in her face. Everywhere she turns, he's there, annoying the fuck out of her. Of course, that can only mean one thing...<br /><br />- - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - -<br /><br />I had a ton of issues with this book. It really was <b>not for me.</b> Mostly though, there was a lot of repetition, everything was far too overdone or OTT for my liking.<br /><br /><b>Hard to believe that Dominic was an 18 year old.</b><br /><b>Bronagh's body issues.</b> I got it, I didn't need to be reminded of it all the time.<br />The violent behaviors in nearly every character... <b>Bronagh slaps and punches and throws things at Dominic, who punches Jason, Gavin headbutts Dominic, Dominic bites Bronagh, Branna punches Dominic and scratches Ryder, Destiny attacks Bronagh and so does Micah....</b> This all really happens, and probably more.<br /><b>Two hundred and seventy odd versions of the word 'fuck'</b> it got a little annoying and pointless.<br />On the mention of repetition, there was <b>100+ eye rolls</b> too. **Eye roll**<br />Even though Dominic declares <b>'she's mine', that does not necessarily mean he's hers.</b> Share the love.<br /><b>'The first time always hurts for girls.'</b> Er... no... it doesn't. - this line later redeemed itself by pointing out that sperm doesn't really taste great. Lol.<br />Then to top it all off I find out that the one guy I liked - Damien - turns out to be a bit of an ass too.<br /><br /><b>I really enjoyed the first 20% it was funny. So I will try the 2nd book, but refrain from rating/reviewing if I don't like it, because it will be my own fault.<br />As for that 20%, I really liked the 'love/hate' storyline, Bronagh was incredibly funny. She was argumentative, silly, kind of violent and sarcastic. Then it just went badly from there out for me, there was far too much of the mentioned above, too much arguing and everything that went with it.</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6537671596004328829"><br/><b>RATING: DNF @ 58% :(</b><br/><br/><i>Dominic</i> just isn’t for me. I can’t connect with the characters nor can I respect them. I realize the blurb warns about all the possible reasons why someone would not like the story but there is a limit. I was expecting a little bit of everything mentioned in the blurb, and I made my peace with all that BEFORE starting, but what I can’t condone is violence, no matter how bad a temper someone has. The heroine has a bad temper - fine. She hits the hero on multiple occasions - NO</span>
  <span id="freeText6537671596004328829" style="display:none"><br /><b>RATING: DNF @ 58% :(</b><br /><br /><i>Dominic</i> just isn’t for me. I can’t connect with the characters nor can I respect them. I realize the blurb warns about all the possible reasons why someone would not like the story but there is a limit. I was expecting a little bit of everything mentioned in the blurb, and I made my peace with all that BEFORE starting, but what I can’t condone is violence, no matter how bad a temper someone has. The heroine has a bad temper - fine. She hits the hero on multiple occasions - NOT fine. Her sister hits the hero on multiple occasions - NOT fine. So, that was my last straw.<br /><br />Maybe its just not the right time for me to read this. There are numerous raving reviews so don’t take my opinion on this. This is just a pinch of my thoughts. <br /><br />Suffice to say, I don’t think I’ll be continuing with the series. <br /><br />#MaybeSomeOtherTime....OrNot<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>

<span id="freeTextContainer1631191965097838317"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*Nope, Just Nope*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote> <br/><b><u>Re-read</u>:</b><br/>The book centers around <b>Bronagh ‘Bee’ Jane Murphy</b> (17, turns 18) and <b>Dominic ‘Nico’ Slater</b> (18). Dominic is new to Bronagh's school and they immediately clash. Already having a bully after her, Bronagh doesn't need another. Specially not one who calls her his own.. Overall I didn't like it. The re-read was a complete bust and I really regret starting it. I wanted to quit straight away, but I kept saying to myself; ‘‘maybe there will be some character gro</span>
  <span id="freeText1631191965097838317" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*Nope, Just Nope*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote> <br><b><u>Re-read</u>:</b><br>The book centers around <b>Bronagh ‘Bee’ Jane Murphy</b> (17, turns 18) and <b>Dominic ‘Nico’ Slater</b> (18). Dominic is new to Bronagh's school and they immediately clash. Already having a bully after her, Bronagh doesn't need another. Specially not one who calls her his own.. Overall I didn't like it. The re-read was a complete bust and I really regret starting it. I wanted to quit straight away, but I kept saying to myself; ‘‘maybe there will be some character growth’’, buuuuuut nooooo. That so did <i>not</i> happen. <br><br>I definitely didn't like the use of faggot and cunt to get back at one another. And I <i>definitely</i> didn't like how Bronagh kept <i>hitting</i> Dominic (Branna too). In fact, they were both quite abusive towards one another; Dominic with his horrible use of words (verbal assaults), and (mostly) Bronagh with use of horrible words <i>and</i> physical abuse/assault. I don't understand how I liked it before, the chemistry is no where to be found and the characters are truly immature and kinda horrible persons. So much that I really didn't want to continue. After 60% I started to skim.<br><br>From the moment I started the book, I knew I wouldn't like it. The constant use of ‘!’ quickly became annoying, Bronagh constant yelling/angry at people who <u>did not</u> deserve it, was eye rolling to read, her ‘all the time temper tantrum’ got boring the first time it happened, and Dominic wasn't all that hot this time around. In fact, I found him childish, immature and kinda...‘abusive’ and seriously lacked control - he had some temperament uses, and big one at that. Though there were moments were Dominic and Bronagh has some cuteness, it never lasted long and it was annoying as fuck. That being said, I no longer like this book. If you hadn't caught that, that is.<br><br><b><u>Other Characters</u>:</b><br><i>The list is somewhat long so I put it in a spoilers tag.</i><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[→ <b>Branna ‘Bran’</b> (28), Bronagh's older sister who became her legal guardian nine years ago when their parents died in a car accident. She's a medical student in her fourth year studying to be a midwife. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Turns out that she and Ryder has been dating for a couple of week not knowing who their siblings were; now a couple. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>→ <b>Alannah ‘Lana’ Ryan</b>, Bronagh's classmate.<br>→ <b>Damien ‘Dame’ Slater</b> (blond-white hair, Dominic has brown hair), Dominic's twin brother. The Slaters just moved from USA, and is new classmates of Bronagh's.<br>→ <b>Mr. Kelly</b>, the woodwork teacher at Bronagh's school.<br>→ <b>Jason Bane</b>, the main (before the Slaters) pretty boy in this school and had always been a dick to Bronagh. The captain of the football team. <br>→ <b>Destiny</b>, classmate of Bronagh's.<br>→ <b>Gavin ‘Gav’ Collins</b>, classmate of Bronagh's.<br>→ <b>Micah Daley</b>, Jason's equally evil girlfriend. Bi.<br>→ <b>Alec Slater</b> (25), Dominic's brother.<br>→ <b>Kane Slater</b> (23), Dominic's brother.<br>→ <b>Ryder ‘Ry’ Slater</b>, Dominic's oldest brother.<br>→ <b>Miss McKesson</b>, a teacher.<br>→ <b>Skull</b>, a bouncer for an underground fighting club called Darkness. He used to have a thing with Brenna ages ago, now he goes out with <b>Aideen Collins</b>, Branna's friend since they were in primary school. She's also Gavin Collin's big sister.<br>→ <b>Drake ‘The Destroyer’</b>, a fighter in the underground fighting club. Dominic beat him, and got his name ‘Rampage’.<br>→ <b>Robert Moore</b>, fellow classmate.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[→ <b>Marco Miles</b>, a drug dealer. Everyone knows of Marco, his name is known all over the world. He is a very bad person the Slater boys' boss. The Slater boys' father was Marco's best friend since they were kids. They were both bad people and started up their empire from scratch. The brothers grew up around violence and that lifestyle not knowing any better. Were treated like princes, and got everything they wanted because of who their dad was. Their lives were a blur up until their mother and father got killed just after the twins' fifteenth birthday. Their dad crossed Marco looking to get some extra money on a drug cartel deal, so Marco had their dad and mom killed before they could take him out. Their mother wasn't any better - loved money. Marco's nephews <b>Trent</b> and <b>Carter</b>. Carter doesn't look like the family at all, but he is evil like them and Trent was even worse. He really was a younger version of Marco in all aspects from looks to personality. He is dead. His death is the reason the Slater brothers is in debt to Marco: the brothers, bar Damien, have certain jobs they do for Marco. Dominic's job is fighting. Damien is singled out because he is the reason why Trent is dead: Damien killed him. Damien broke after their parents deaths and became violent, Dominic believes Damien barely loves him, but he's gotten better after the move. <b>Nala</b>, Damien's ex girlfriend. Kane is Marco's debt collector and what Marco calls his bruiser. Alec fucks Marco's problems away, literally: is an escort for Marco's clients, Bronagh. Usually the wives or husband of his clients, his job is to keep them happy. Is bisexual. Ryder runs drugs and weapons for Marco, so he is technically a drug and weapons dealer. And Damien does nothing, he isn't involved with Marco. It's part of the deal to keep him safe. He keeps out of everything while the other brothers deal with it. Turns out, Marco lied about Trent being dead to keep the brothers working for him. He's very much alive. The one Marco had buried in his grave was Nala; Trent raped and killed her. She was ten weeks pregnant with Damien's child. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> &lt;--- **LONG AND FULL OF SPOILERS!!!**  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b><u>Quick basic facts</u>:</b><br><b>Genre</b>: - (New Adult) Contemporary Romance (M/F).<br><b>Series</b>: - Series, Book One.<br><b>Love triangle?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Cheating?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>HEA?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes, for the couple <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Favorite character?</b> - None, but if I had to choose; Dominic ‘Nico’ Slater.<br><b>Would I read more by this author/or of series?</b> - Unsure, but probably not anymore.<br><b>Would I recommend this book/series?</b> - Not really.<br><b>Will I read this again in the future?</b> - No.<br><b>New Rating</b> - 2 stars.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445268775i/16623124.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b><u>First read review</u>:</b><br>Not bad, I liked it.<br><b>Rate: 4/3 stars.</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="Yessi Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18300956-yessi-smith"><img alt="Yessi Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442952275p2/18300956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/821141322?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yessi Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yessi Smith" href="/user/show/18300956-yessi-smith">Yessi Smith</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer821141322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6457643936050402002">This is easily the hardest review I’ve written simply because I want to do this book justice. But here goes. <br/><br/>Dominic is more than a story about love and loss, but also a story about trust and letting go.<br/><br/>Bronagh lost her parents when she was nine, leaving her sister Branna as her guardian and the only person she loves and trusts. At 18, Bronagh has built a barrier around herself and her heart that no one has been able to break through. At least until Dominic, an American prick, comes into this sp</span>
  <span id="freeText6457643936050402002" style="display:none">This is easily the hardest review I’ve written simply because I want to do this book justice. But here goes. <br /><br />Dominic is more than a story about love and loss, but also a story about trust and letting go.<br /><br />Bronagh lost her parents when she was nine, leaving her sister Branna as her guardian and the only person she loves and trusts. At 18, Bronagh has built a barrier around herself and her heart that no one has been able to break through. At least until Dominic, an American prick, comes into this spunky Irish lass’ life and very literally turns her world on its heels. Under Dominic’s attentive eye and constant teasing, Bronagh is no longer invisible to her fellow classmates and even finds herself making friends.<br /><br />They share a love/hate relationship that left me smiling and laughing like a moron. I can’t tell you how many times Dominic got clocked in the head, but I enjoyed every single hit, smack and verbal combat between Bronagh and Dominic. Just when Bronagh readies herself to open her heart to this beautiful but arrogant SOB, life throws one more twist at her. A secret Dominic and the other Slater brothers are hiding that explains what brought them to Ireland in the first place.<br /><br />The wit, humor and sarcasm in this book, mixed with the panty dropping sex scenes, makes Dominic a top 5 book for me. Not just a top 5 for 2014, but top 5, ever. So grab your copy and get to know the sexy Slater brothers, who will make you rethink the foundation you’ve built for book boyfriends. <br /><br />Now, um, Ms. L.A. Casey, please hurry so we can read about the rest of Slater brothers, specifically Damien!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1624295849460971507">This is the definition of huge disappointment. I was so ready for a good contemporary romance but I didn't get that. What I got was a huge disappointment!<br/><br/>I didn't too much care for Bronagh but my biggest problem with this story was Dominic. Anyone who thinks he's book boyfriend material has a problem.<br/><br/>I know now days most books have an "alpha male" and yes I like some of those alpha males. But Dominic isn't an alpha male he's a douchelord!<br/><br/>First off he's a bully. He does stuff on purpose just to p</span>
  <span id="freeText1624295849460971507" style="display:none">This is the definition of huge disappointment. I was so ready for a good contemporary romance but I didn't get that. What I got was a huge disappointment!<br /><br />I didn't too much care for Bronagh but my biggest problem with this story was Dominic. Anyone who thinks he's book boyfriend material has a problem.<br /><br />I know now days most books have an "alpha male" and yes I like some of those alpha males. But Dominic isn't an alpha male he's a douchelord!<br /><br />First off he's a bully. He does stuff on purpose just to piss Bronagh off, he picks at her, makes fun of her, and he starts rumors about her. She's told him to leave her alone plenty of times but he doesn't. I don't know about you but that sounds like a bully to me. <b>And I hate bullies!</b> What makes it even worst is that he beats up a guy who does the same thing he does and we're suppose to think of him as a hero ... <b>Child Please!</b><br /><br />Second he's so disrespectful. I don't know how many times he's called Bronagh a bitch. He touches her butt like it's okay for guys to just go around doing that. And he grabs her and says the most disgusting things ever. But I guess that's supposed to be sexy too. <br /><br />Third he has a huge anger problem! It seems like he was suppose to be like Travis Maddox. Don't get me wrong I know Travis Maddox had an anger problem too. But if you hate Travis Maddox you should seriously hate this guy. He makes Travis look like an angel. <br /><br />I can go on and on about how disgusting Dominic is and how much I hate him but it's pointless because you will have your on opinion of him. Just know you've been warned. <br /><br />I couldn't even finish the story because I couldn't stop rolling my eyes. I don't usually rate stories I don't finish but I really hated this book and I will not continue with this series.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18322423711991434375">This book is honestly not for everyone. When I read a bunch of reviews I was very hesitant about giving it a try. I will admit that this book kept me interested...I am a bit embarrassed by that considering it was more like a drama filled soap opera. I obviously still have some part of me that enjoys the drama filled life of others!!! Seeing as this is not real and just a story, I was able to sit back and just enjoy.<br/><br/>The Slater brothers are definitely as alpha as they come. They have moved to Irel</span>
  <span id="freeText18322423711991434375" style="display:none">This book is honestly not for everyone. When I read a bunch of reviews I was very hesitant about giving it a try. I will admit that this book kept me interested...I am a bit embarrassed by that considering it was more like a drama filled soap opera. I obviously still have some part of me that enjoys the drama filled life of others!!! Seeing as this is not real and just a story, I was able to sit back and just enjoy.<br /><br />The Slater brothers are definitely as alpha as they come. They have moved to Ireland with plenty of secrets following. This first book in the series is about Dominic, who ends up falling in love with an Irish girl named; Bronagh. She is a very feisty heroine, and fore warning....their way of dealing with each other is usually Bronagh slapping him around and different play fighting tactics. On know a lot of readers were put off by the physical aspect in how Bronagh and her sister dealt with the guys. I took it with a grain of salt, only because most of the time it was a ton of playing around...as well as Dominic never felt abused by her, he more called her behaviour "foreplay." That is the vibe I mainly got as well, so I took it for that!<br /><br />There is never a dull moment in this book, and emotions are always running very high. Dominic and Bronagh are in high school, and believe me; this story has a very high school feel to it.<br />So, if you are not into a ton of drama, and even more juvenile behaviour...then this book is probably not for you! For me, I have to be in the right head space for it...but their antics kept me interested and entertained.. I will call this series my guilty indulgence and leave it at that! LOL</span>

  <span id="freeText5243885505165892370" style="display:none">I read Ryder first before I read Dominic. Listening to this book is like walking on a memory lane in my high school. The banter between Dominic and Bronagh is cute. Really cute. I love Dominic. He is such a tease and smart mouth. Usually the heroine is the sassy mouth, but on Dominic, the hero is the sassy mouth. <br /><br />Dominic is my favorite hero on this series so far. On the other hand, Bronagh... Bronagh is the reason I give this book 3 stars. <br /><br />3 stars</span>

<div id="review_2280045219" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2280045219" />
    <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga"><img alt="Beatrice Masaluñga" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603719912p2/4590441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2280045219?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beatrice Masaluñga" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga">Beatrice Masaluñga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2280045219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3745707168326981440">I don't know where I got my long patience and manage to finish this book. I picked this up out on a whim because I'm in the mood for angsty read. However, I didn't expect to deal with incredibly annoying characters and their over the fucking top drama. I've encountered books with bullies/jerk heroes like Jared Trent (Bully), Reed Royal (Paper Princess), Caine Carraway (Hero) etc.. They have reasons why they're acting like assholes. I find these guys redeemable and ended up loving them. In this b</span>
  <span id="freeText3745707168326981440" style="display:none">I don't know where I got my long patience and manage to finish this book. I picked this up out on a whim because I'm in the mood for angsty read. However, I didn't expect to deal with incredibly annoying characters and their over the fucking top drama. I've encountered books with bullies/jerk heroes like Jared Trent (Bully), Reed Royal (Paper Princess), Caine Carraway (Hero) etc.. They have reasons why they're acting like assholes. I find these guys redeemable and ended up loving them. In this book, that wasn't the case because I despise the hero even his love interest. <u>Kindly bear with me because this is going to be a rant review.</u><br /><br /><b><u>Reasons why I hate this book:</u> </b><br /><br />1.<b>The Heroine: Bronagh Murphy</b> - I understand her issue on being closed-off to everyone since her parents died when she's a kid and her older sister became her guardian. She's bullied in school and I've got to admit they're all assholes and bitches. It's just that I can't stand her attitude. She acts like a toddler and her temper tantrums pissed me off! Goodness, she's mad all the time and needs to take a chill pill. She's childish, uptight and too sarcastic. She's a wannabe tough chick but she can't even stand on her own. If throwing a lot of profanity makes her feisty, I don't think so. 😒🔪<br /><br />2. <b>The Hero: Dominic Slater</b> - AHA! This arrogant, rude, slut-shaming and misogynistic idiot. 🙄 He has no respect for women and I hate him for calling Bronagh and he gets jealous and territorial on her when weren't even dating <i>yet</i>. I hate whenever he touches her butt and call it "fat ass". I don't care he's popular and sexy but his attitude is a complete turn off. I hate him even more when he said "I think all Asians like light skin and hair." This generalization needs to die ASAP.. Bye dude! ✋🏼😒<br /><br />3. <b>Romance = Toxic Relationship </b> - There is nothing romantic between Bronagh and Dominic. They have nonstop bickering and fight over the pettiest things. May I note Dominic here: CALLING YOUR GF A "BITCH" ISN'T SEXY NOR ROMANTIC! 😡 These two have goo-goo eyes for each other yet throw insulting endearments. I'm appalled.<br /><br />4. <b> Plot.</b> - Nothing much happened until the last 20% of the book. 80% of it will just test your patience.<br /><br />Overall, I dislike it but I'm continuing the series and crossing my fingers for improvement. This series needs a redemption and I just hope it's less annoying. No more migraine inducing drama please!</span>

  <span id="freeText12350699057289836622" style="display:none">Soo I have read this book a moth ago .. Why it took so long to make a review you ask? Well ... I'm asking the same damn question. Even after all this time, I'm not sure what I'm feeling about this book. But I need to say something - I have read this book in one sitting. I couldn't stop. I really wanted to know what was gonna happen. That's a good thing, no?<br /><br />Ok. Now for my thoughts. It may contain spoilers so it's on your own risk.<br /><br />The book was fun and light. I liked the banter between the characters. After the big fight they had, and the harsh words they told each other, the whole kidnapping fiasco happens and after that they are together again. Without TALKING about the fight. <br /><br />Through all the book I felt they didn't TALK !! I wanted them to discuss and to talk about things, to show some emotions .. But I didn't felt it. <div id="review_843723675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/843723675" />
    <a title="Silla Webb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17041467-silla-webb"><img alt="Silla Webb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562042226p2/17041467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/843723675?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silla Webb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silla Webb" href="/user/show/17041467-silla-webb">Silla Webb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer843723675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8296784864693744276">WOW...I seriously am just blown away...debut release? NO...no way in hell, that this 22 year old young momma wrote this...YES...YES SHE DID!!! <br/><br/>L.A. Casey is a new author, releasing her debut novel Dominic on March 17, 2014. I received a copy of Dominic to BETA read, pre release. WOW...<br/><br/>Bronagh Murphy is a senior in high school, living with her older sister. Still coping with the death of her parents, ten years earlier, Bronagh would love nothing more than to fade away from her own existence. She </span>
  <span id="freeText8296784864693744276" style="display:none">WOW...I seriously am just blown away...debut release? NO...no way in hell, that this 22 year old young momma wrote this...YES...YES SHE DID!!! <br /><br />L.A. Casey is a new author, releasing her debut novel Dominic on March 17, 2014. I received a copy of Dominic to BETA read, pre release. WOW...<br /><br />Bronagh Murphy is a senior in high school, living with her older sister. Still coping with the death of her parents, ten years earlier, Bronagh would love nothing more than to fade away from her own existence. She lives in a bubble...a state of solitude. Nobody notices her, and she prefers it that way. That is until the Slater Brothers move to town. Bronagh has her first experience with the devilishly sexy twins during her morning registration class, when they take her seat, then Dominic, being the prick that he is makes a fuss about having to move. When Bronagh cuts back at him with her smart ass words, he becomes determined that she will be his...and what Dominic wants...Dominic gets...can Dominic want me, PLEASE!!!! <br /><br />Their relationship goes cat and mouse, back and forth for a while, with the constant I hate yous, etc, but Dominic is always there, protecting Bronagh when she needs it most. But did she really need protecting? No...but everyone thought since she was always the loner, that shew was ready to crack, she was fragile...she just needed someone to work their way in, and show her that it was okay to love again. In reality, Bronagh is a hell of a lot stronger than what Branna, her friends, or the brothers ever imagined...but she pulls her strength from down deep within herself, and fights back, when the time calls for it. She protects her family, refuses to back down, and fights to live, fights for love. <br /><br />**********************************************************************<br /><br />L.A. Casey writes amazingly beautiful...her characters mesh so well...Bronagh and Dominic are the perfect case of hormonal bitches, which is why they hate/love each other so much...they mirror each other. Both are bitchy, mean and will fight for what they want. I literally laughed my ass off at so many lines all throughout the book. It was filled with humor, playful banter. One specific scene, (I won't spoil) was so beautifully written, I was blown away. Every word in that chapter was perfect, from the sweetest to the most devious. I felt so much emotion reading through Dominic, there were twists and turns I truly did NOT expect...I was really expecting a Coming of Age Romance, but this book is MORE...it is deeper. It is REAL...there is love, hate, sex...steamy sex, there is fear and gut wrenching heart ache. I seriously want to fly to friggin' Dublin, and find L.A. Casey, and hug her neck, then slap her arse, because this book, has blown me away, and left me completely hungover, drunk, and ready for more of the Slater Brothers!!!! Can I give it a 10* PLEASE!!!!! <br /><br /><br />LA CASEY<br />CR-<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bit.ly/1lk9hzW">http://bit.ly/1lk9hzW</a><br />BT-<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bit.ly/1k9gfGz">http://bit.ly/1k9gfGz</a><br />GR-<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bit.ly/1cq1bAi">http://bit.ly/1cq1bAi</a><br />Release Event~<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/events/1445803545650697/">https://www.facebook.com/events/14458...</a><br /><br />Contributions:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bit.ly/1egaJtD">http://bit.ly/1egaJtD</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8296784864693744276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText2838287952746700520" style="display:none">I’M SO ASHAMED!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504282623ra/23739953.gif" alt="description/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Where is my banner of feminism and gender equality?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504282623ra/23739952.gif" alt="description/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Why did I enjoy this book so much? The Hero was the stereotypical good looking, strong, can’t nobody beat him male<br>4.	The Heroine hid behind the Hero and had him fight her battles<br>5.	The Heroine would run her mouth, but couldn’t back up her words <br>6.	The Heroine beat on the Hero often<br>7.	The Hero had an unrealistic temper<br><br><br>But I really liked it!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495340330ra/22808552.gif" alt="description/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Yes, Dominic fit the typical dominant male role and Bronagh fit the typical weak role, but shhh….I want more! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504282623ra/23739954.gif" alt="description/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Dominic is one of 5 male siblings and of course all his brothers are HOT! Their profession makes them dangerous and alluring. Dominic met Bronagh at school and pulled her out of her self-induced shell by bullying her. Even though Dominic bullied her, he protected her from getting bullied by others. Once Bronagh accepted that she belonged to Dominic a beautiful romance began. <br><br>Yes, I plan to read the next one while hiding in my closet under a pile of clothes. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504282623ra/23739951.gif" alt="description/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('g/Wk+KUw7U9qVOIkLGePit8iboF3dr/UuO3vlfwXbS05dBsg/jCaOXalfzWp6J7V7lZXhIoBHOEA/B5aAAdFUg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('H4m42b9Q90rKnsHljV5KlQTONgrFTbjOrE+X73S2KZalCAcB5FCAPNZvXPQI0VvKNboPDzg6G/sUXmYgiKYB6Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText5453193552362190009" style="display:none">L.A. Casey is a <i>New York Times</i> and <i>USA Today</i> bestselling author who juggles her time between her mini-me and writing.
